- Use `github.com/sg-evals/node--v22.13.0` as the `repo` parameter for go_to_definition/find_references/read_file


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Node.js child_process Command Injection Guards

## Your Task

Find all JavaScript and C++ source files in nodejs/node that implement input validation and command injection prevention for the child_process module. Identify: the normalizeSpawnArguments function with null-byte validation, the exec/execFile/spawn entry points, the internal ChildProcess class that interfaces with C++, the ProcessWrap native binding, and the validator functions (validateArgumentNullCheck) used to prevent injection.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the security domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/node--v22.13.0.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/node--v22.13.0` (nodejs/node)

## Summary

I have successfully identified and documented all the command injection prevention components in Node.js's child_process module. The comprehensive findings have been saved to `/workspace/answer.json`.

### Key Findings:

**JavaScript Layer (lib/child_process.js):**
- **validateArgumentNullCheck()** - Core security function that rejects strings containing null bytes (\u0000), preventing null byte injection attacks
- **validateArgumentsNullCheck()** - Validates all arguments in arrays for null bytes
- **normalizeSpawnArguments()** - Normalizes spawn arguments and validates file, args, argv0, shell, and environment variables for null bytes
- **Entry points**: spawn(), fork(), exec(), execFile(), execSync(), execFileSync(), spawnSync()

**Internal Implementation (lib/internal/child_process.js):**
- **ChildProcess class** - Internal wrapper that interfaces between JavaScript and C++ ProcessWrap
- **ChildProcess.prototype.spawn()** - Calls the native C++ spawn implementation
- **setupChannel()** - Establishes IPC for fork operations

**Native C++ Binding (src/process_wrap.cc):**
- **ProcessWrap class** - Native binding to libuv process operations
- **ProcessWrap::Spawn()** - Validates options, processes arguments/environment, performs **IsWindowsBatchFile()** check to prevent Windows batch file execution
- **ProcessWrap::Kill()** - Terminates processes

**Additional Security:**
- **IsWindowsBatchFile()** (src/util-inl.h) - Windows-specific security check preventing batch file exploitation
- **ChildProcessPermission** (src/permission/child_process_permission.h/cc) - Permission system enforcing restrictions on child process spawning

The complete documentation with file paths, symbols, call chains, and detailed explanations is available in `/workspace/answer.json`.
